## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration in such systems typically depends on restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force plus damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping term)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Combined quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2 + c2)**(-0.5) (nonlinear friction model)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling between x and v)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal external forcing)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power restoring forces (x**2) → asymmetric potential wells causing drift or asymmetric oscillations
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/antidamping)
- Terms like (1 - x**2)*v → amplitude-dependent damping causing limit cycle behavior (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Cubic position term x**3 → hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring nonlinearity
- Product terms x*v → nonlinear coupling between position and velocity indicating non-conservative forces
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence indicates non-autonomous/driven system

`-0.424310587218182*v*(1 - x²) - 1.92728910930903*x*(0.0682163475684738*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 1.92728910930903*x + 0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x²`
- `-1.92728910930903*0.0682163475684738*x*|v|^(1/3) - 1.92728910930903*x`
- `-1.92728910930903*x`
- `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

Combining:
`0.30645527626767*sin(t) - 3.85457821861806*x - 0.424310587218182*v + 0.424310587218182*v*x² - 0.131504932985*x*|v|^(1/3)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
1. `sin(t)`
2. `x`
3. `v`
4. `v*x²`
5. `x*|v|^(1/3)`

The key distinguishing term is `x*|v|^(1/3)`. Let me check each candidate for this.

**Candidates with `|v|^(1/3)` or equivalent:**
- Candidate 5: has `v^c6*x` → set c6=1/3, but this gives `v^(1/3)*x`, not `|v|^(1/3)*x`. Since v takes both signs, `v^(1/3)` is not the same as `|v|^(1/3)` (one is odd, the other is even in sign).
- Candidate 35: has `x*(c7+v)^(1/3)` — this is `(c7+v)^(1/3)`, not `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with `log(|v|)` terms:** Candidates 1, 2 — `log` is not `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with `sqrt(v)` terms:** Candidates 2,3,4,6,8,9,10,18,19,20,23,34 — `sqrt(c+v)` is not `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with `sin(c*t)`, `cos(c*t)`, or `v*sin/cos` terms:** These add time-dependent basis functions not in GT. Setting coefficients to 0 would remove them, but then the `|v|^(1/3)*x` term would be missing.

**Candidates with polynomial-only v terms (v², v³, x³, x⁵):** These cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with `exp(c*x)`:** Cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with `sin(c*(c*x + c*v))`:** Cannot produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

Let me systematically verify: The GT requires the term `x*|v|^(1/3)` which is a specific nonlinear basis function. None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `Abs(v)^(1/3)` explicitly.

Candidate 5 has `v^c6*x` — if we set c6=1/3, we get `v^(1/3)*x`. But v takes both positive and negative values, and `v^(1/3)` (real cube root) gives negative values for negative v, while `|v|^(1/3)` is always non-negative. These are different functions. **No match.**

Candidate 1 has `x*log(c6*|v|+1)` — log is not a power function. **No match.**

Going through all 52 candidates: None contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `Abs(v)^c` with a fractional exponent that preserves the absolute value. The critical basis function `x*|v|^(1/3)` cannot be reproduced by any candidate.
